### Assistant

Perfect! Now I understand the warnings. Let me summarize what I found:

## System Health Warnings Analysis

**The 2 warnings detected are:**

### Warning 1 & 2: VKB Server Unavailable (duplicate detection)
- **Check**: `vkb_server`
- **Status**: error (severity: warning)
- **Endpoint**: http://localhost:8080/health
- **Issue**: VKB server is NOT running
- **Auto-heal**: Enabled (action: restart_vkb_server)

The health verification system ran the check twice, creating duplicate violation entries for the same issue.

**Verification:**
```bash
$ lsof -i :8080
# (empty - VKB not running)
```

## Why This Is Happening

The VKB server was NOT started when we started this Claude session because:
1. VKB typically starts via `start-services.sh`
2. But we're continuing from a previous session
3. VKB must have crashed or was stopped earlier

## Resolution

Let me start the VKB server now:

**Tool:** Bash
**Input:** ```json

  "description": "Start VKB server on port 8080"
}
```

### Assistant



### Assistant

Found it! The issue is in the `getSemanticStatus()` method in `combined-status-line.js`. It's checking the wrong field.

**The Problem:**
```javascript
// Line 347 - checks services array (but semantic-analysis is never added there)
const hasSemanticAnalysis = services.services.includes('semantic-analysis');
```

**But the actual data structure is:**
```json
{
  "services": ["transcript-monitor", "live-logging-coordinator", ...],
  "semantic_analysis": {  // â† Separate object, not in array
    "status": "âœ… OPERATIONAL",
    "health": "healthy"
  }
}
```

Let me fix the getSemanticStatus method:

## âœ… API Warning FIXED!

**Status Line Before:**
```
[ğŸ§ APIâš ï¸]  â† Warning
```

**Status Line After:**
```
[ğŸ§ APIâœ…]  â† All clear!
```

### Root Cause

The `getSemanticStatus()` method in `combined-status-line.js` was checking the wrong field:

**Bug (line 347):**
```javascript
const hasSemanticAnalysis = services.services.includes('semantic-analysis');
```

This checked if "semantic-analysis" was in the `services` array, but it never gets added there because the Semantic Analysis MCP Server uses **stdio transport** (not HTTP), so it's tracked differently.

**Actual data structure in `.services-running.json`:**
```json
{
  "services": ["transcript-monitor", "vkb-server", ...],  // â† Never includes semantic-analysis
  "semantic_analysis": {  // â† Separate object
    "status": "âœ… OPERATIONAL",
    "health": "healthy"
  }
}
```

### Fix Applied

Changed `getSemanticStatus()` to check the `semantic_analysis` object directly (lines 348-357):

```javascript
const semanticAnalysis = services.semantic_analysis;

if (semanticAnalysis && semanticAnalysis.health === 'healthy') {
  return { status: 'operational' };  // â†’ Shows [ğŸ§ APIâœ…]
}
```

### All Warnings Now Cleared

Your status line now shows:
- `[ğŸ§ APIâœ…]` - Semantic Analysis API healthy âœ…
- `[ğŸ”âœ…]` - System Health verification all clear âœ…
- VKB server running on port 8080 âœ…

**Modified file:** `scripts/combined-status-line.js:338-361`

## 1. Primary Request and Intent

The user's requests in chronological order:
1. **System Health Dashboard startup issue**: Investigate why the system health dashboard (port 3032) is not running and ensure it starts reliably when `coding/bin/coding` is launched for the first session

6. **Documentation update**: Update documentation to reflect the new health emoji on the status line

## 2. Key Technical Concepts

- **System Health Dashboard Architecture**: Two-component system
  - API Server (Express.js on port 3033) - provides health verification data
  - Dashboard Frontend (Vite/React on port 3032) - displays monitoring interface
- **Service Startup Chain**: `bin/coding` â†’ `scripts/launch-claude.sh` â†’ `start-services.sh`
- **Process State Manager**: Registers services for tracking
- **Health Verification System**: Layer 3 monitoring with auto-healing
- **Status Line Indicators**: Combined status line showing various service states
- **`.services-running.json` Structure**: Service tracking with separate objects for stdio-based services like `semantic_analysis`
- **Port Configuration**: Centralized in `.env.ports` file
- **Auto-persist vs Event-driven Export**: Different mechanisms for data persistence

### `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/start-services.sh`
**Why important**: This is the main service startup script called by `launch-claude.sh` - controls which services auto-start when coding sessions begin.

**Code added (lines 409-447)**:
```bash
# Start System Health Dashboard (API + Frontend)
echo "ğŸŸ¢ Starting System Health Dashboard..."
cd "$CODING_DIR/integrations/system-health-dashboard"

# Check if dependencies are installed
if [ ! -d "node_modules" ]; then
    echo "   ğŸ“¦ Installing System Health Dashboard dependencies..."
    npm install --silent 2>/dev/null || pnpm install --silent 2>/dev/null || {
        echo "   âš ï¸ Failed to install dependencies - System Health Dashboard will be unavailable"
        HEALTH_API_PID="not-installed"
        HEALTH_DASHBOARD_PID="not-installed"
    }
fi

if [ "$HEALTH_API_PID" != "not-installed" ]; then
    # Load port configuration from .env.ports
    if [ -f "$CODING_DIR/.env.ports" ]; then
        export $(grep '^SYSTEM_HEALTH_' "$CODING_DIR/.env.ports" | sed 's/#.*//' | xargs)
    fi

    # Start the API server in background (port 3033)
    SYSTEM_HEALTH_API_PORT=${SYSTEM_HEALTH_API_PORT:-3033} nohup npm run api > "$CODING_DIR/logs/system-health-api.log" 2>&1 &
    HEALTH_API_PID=$!
    echo "   System Health API PID: $HEALTH_API_PID (port 3033)"

    # Start the dashboard frontend in background (port 3032)
    SYSTEM_HEALTH_DASHBOARD_PORT=${SYSTEM_HEALTH_DASHBOARD_PORT:-3032} nohup npm run dev > "$CODING_DIR/logs/system-health-dashboard.log" 2>&1 &
    HEALTH_DASHBOARD_PID=$!
    echo "   System Health Dashboard PID: $HEALTH_DASHBOARD_PID (port 3032)"

    # Register with Process State Manager
    cd "$CODING_DIR"
    node scripts/psm-register.js system-health-api $HEALTH_API_PID global integrations/system-health-dashboard/server.js 2>/dev/null || true
    node scripts/psm-register.js system-health-dashboard $HEALTH_DASHBOARD_PID global integrations/system-health-dashboard 2>/dev/null || true
else
    echo "   âš ï¸ System Health Dashboard not available"
fi
```

### `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/scripts/combined-status-line.js`

**Why important**: Generates the status line shown in prompts - critical for monitoring system health at a glance.

**Bug fix in `getSemanticStatus()` method (lines 338-361)**:
```javascript
async getSemanticStatus() {
  try {
    // Check MCP semantic analysis connection
    const servicesPath = join(rootDir, '.services-running.json');
    if (!existsSync(servicesPath)) {
      return { status: 'offline' };
    }

    const services = JSON.parse(readFileSync(servicesPath, 'utf8'));

    // Check semantic_analysis object (not in services array because it uses stdio transport)
    const semanticAnalysis = services.semantic_analysis;

    if (semanticAnalysis && semanticAnalysis.health === 'healthy') {
      return { status: 'operational' };
    } else if (semanticAnalysis) {
      return { status: 'degraded' };
    } else {
      return { status: 'offline' };
    }
  } catch (error) {
    return { status: 'offline', error: error.message };
  }
}
```

**Icon change - Health Verifier Status (lines 1239-1265)**:
```javascript
// Health Verifier Status (Hospital/medical icon for health monitoring)
if (healthVerifier && healthVerifier.status === 'operational') {
  const overallStatus = healthVerifier.overallStatus || 'healthy';
  const violationCount = healthVerifier.violationCount || 0;
  const criticalCount = healthVerifier.criticalCount || 0;

  if (criticalCount > 0) {
    parts.push(`[ğŸ¥âŒ${criticalCount}]`); // Critical issues
    overallColor = 'red';
  } else if (violationCount > 0) {
    parts.push(`[ğŸ¥âš ï¸${violationCount}]`); // Warning issues
    if (overallColor === 'green') overallColor = 'yellow';
  } else if (overallStatus === 'healthy') {
    parts.push('[ğŸ¥âœ…]'); // All checks passed
  } else {
    parts.push('[ğŸ¥ğŸŸ¡]'); // Degraded but no specific violations
    if (overallColor === 'green') overallColor = 'yellow';
  }
} else if (healthVerifier && healthVerifier.status === 'stale') {
  parts.push('[ğŸ¥â°]'); // Stale data
  if (overallColor === 'green') overallColor = 'yellow';
} else if (healthVerifier && healthVerifier.status === 'error') {
  parts.push('[ğŸ¥âŒ]'); // Error reading status
  if (overallColor === 'green') overallColor = 'yellow';
} else {
  parts.push('[ğŸ¥ğŸ’¤]'); // Offline/not running
}
```

## 4. Errors and Fixes

### Error 1: Dashboard Frontend Not Starting
**Error**: Only API server (port 3033) was added to startup, but dashboard frontend (port 3032) wasn't running.

**User feedback**: "the health dashboard is not showing (should this be on localhost:3032?)"

**Fix**: 
- Added second startup command for dashboard frontend using `npm run dev`
- Added verification check for port 3032
- Updated service counts from 5 to 6 (and 7 to 8 with constraint monitor)
- Added dashboard log file to summary

### Error 2: API Warning - Semantic Status Bug
**Error**: Status line showed `[ğŸ§ APIâš ï¸]` because `getSemanticStatus()` was checking wrong field.

**Root cause**: Line 347 checked `services.services.includes('semantic-analysis')` but semantic-analysis is stored as separate object `semantic_analysis` in `.services-running.json` because it uses stdio transport (not HTTP).

**Fix**: Changed to check `services.semantic_analysis` object directly and verify `health === 'healthy'`.

**Result**: Status line now shows `[ğŸ§ APIâœ…]`

### Error 3: VKB Server Not Running
**Error**: Health verifier showed 2 warnings - both "vkb_server is unavailable" on port 8080.

**Root cause**: VKB server wasn't started in this continued session (likely crashed earlier).

**Fix**: Started VKB server manually:
```bash
cd /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding && nohup node lib/vkb-server/cli.js server start --foreground > vkb-server.log 2>&1 &
```

**Result**: Health status changed to `violationCount: 0`, status line shows `[ğŸ¥âœ…]`

### Error 4: Wrong Directory for VKB Start
**Error**: First attempt to start VKB failed because command was run from `integrations/system-health-dashboard` directory.

**Fix**: Changed to absolute path `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding` before starting VKB server.

     3â†’## Overview
     4â†’
     5â†’The Claude Code status line system provides real-time monitoring of the development environment through a modular, service-oriented architecture. The system aggregates status information from multiple independent services and presents it as a unified, color-coded status display.

     8â†’

    10â†’
    11â†’**Key Features**:

   118â†’- `idle` - Session exists but not actively streaming exchanges
   119â†’- `stale` - Health data is slightly outdated (90s-2min old)
   120â†’- `old` - Health data is too old (2min-6hrs)

     1â†’# Health Verification System
     2â†’
     3â†’Automatic system health verification that runs on every Claude prompt, ensuring a stable and self-healing development environment.
     4â†’
     5â†’## Overview
     6â†’
     7â†’The Health Verification System provides **failsafe monitoring** with three key features:
     8â†’1. **Pre-Prompt Health Checks** - Verifies system health before every Claude prompt
     9â†’2. **Self-Monitoring** - The health system monitors itself
    10â†’3. **Auto-Healing** - Automatically restarts failed services
    11â†’
    12â†’## Architecture
    13â†’
    14â†’![Health Verification Flow](../images/health-verification-flow.png)
    15â†’
    16â†’The diagram shows the complete flow from user prompt to health verification:
    17â†’
    18â†’1. **User types prompt** â†’ Claude Code receives it
    19â†’2. **UserPromptSubmit hook fires** â†’ Executes health-prompt-hook.js
    20â†’3. **Hook checks status file** â†’ Reads .health/verification-status.json
    21â†’4. **If data is fresh** (<5 min) â†’ Returns health context immediately
    22â†’5. **If data is stale** (>5 min) â†’ Spawns async verification + returns "refreshing" context
    23â†’6. **Background verification** â†’ Checks all services, auto-heals failures, updates status
    24â†’7. **Claude receives context** â†’ Prompt processed with health information
    25â†’
    26â†’## Components
    27â†’
    28â†’### 1. Pre-Prompt Hook
    29â†’
    30â†’**File**: `scripts/health-prompt-hook.js`
    31â†’
    32â†’**Trigger**: Every Claude prompt (via UserPromptSubmit hook)
    33â†’
    34â†’**Behavior**:
    35â†’- Checks if `.health/verification-status.json` is fresh (<5 minutes)
    36â†’- If stale: Spawns async health verification (doesn't wait)
    37â†’- Provides health status as additional context to Claude
    38â†’- Blocks prompt only if critical failures are active
    39â†’
    40â†’**Output Format**:
    41â†’```json
    42â†’{
    43â†’  "hookSpecificOutput": {
    44â†’    "hookEventName": "UserPromptSubmit",
    45â†’    "additionalContext": "âœ… System Health: All systems operational (verified 23s ago)\n"
    46â†’  }
    47â†’}
    48â†’```
    49â†’
    50â†’### 2. Health Verifier
    51â†’
    52â†’**File**: `scripts/health-verifier.js`
    53â†’
    54â†’**Checks**:
    55â†’- **Databases**: LevelDB locks, Qdrant availability, graph integrity
    56â†’- **Services**: VKB server, constraint monitor, dashboard server, **health API** (self-monitoring)
    57â†’- **Processes**: Stale PIDs, zombie processes, resource usage
    58â†’
    59â†’**Self-Monitoring Check**:
    60â†’```json
    61â†’{
    62â†’  "health_dashboard_api": {
    63â†’    "enabled": true,
    64â†’    "severity": "error",
    65â†’    "check_type": "http_health",
    66â†’    "endpoint": "http://localhost:3033/api/health",
    67â†’    "auto_heal": true,
    68â†’    "auto_heal_action": "restart_health_api"
    69â†’  }
    70â†’}
    71â†’```
    72â†’
    73â†’The health system verifies its own API server is running and auto-heals if down.
    74â†’
    75â†’### 3. Auto-Healing
    76â†’
    77â†’**File**: `scripts/health-remediation-actions.js`
    78â†’
    79â†’**Actions**:
    80â†’- `restart_vkb_server` - Restart VKB visualization server
    81â†’- `restart_constraint_monitor` - Restart constraint monitoring API
    82â†’- `restart_dashboard_server` - Restart constraint dashboard
    83â†’- `restart_health_api` - Restart health API server (self-healing)
    84â†’- `start_qdrant` - Start Qdrant Docker container
    85â†’- `kill_lock_holder` - Kill process holding LevelDB lock
    86â†’- `cleanup_dead_processes` - Remove stale PID registrations
    87â†’- `cleanup_zombies` - Clean up zombie processes
    88â†’
    89â†’### 4. System Health Dashboard
    90â†’
    91â†’**Location**: `integrations/system-health-dashboard/`
    92â†’
    93â†’**Ports**:
    94â†’- Frontend: `http://localhost:3032` (Vite + React)
    95â†’- Backend API: `http://localhost:3033` (Express)
    96â†’
    97â†’**Features**:
    98â†’- Real-time monitoring (5s refresh via WebSocket)
    99â†’- Database, service, and process health
   100â†’- Violation history and recommendations
   101â†’- Manual verification trigger
   102â†’- Auto-healing status
   103â†’
   104â†’## Configuration
   105â†’
   106â†’### Hook Setup
   107â†’
   108â†’Add to `~/.claude/settings.json`:
   109â†’
   110â†’```json
   111â†’{
   112â†’  "hooks": {
   113â†’    "UserPromptSubmit": [
   114â†’      {
   115â†’        "hooks": [
   116â†’          {
   117â†’            "type": "command",
   118â†’            "command": "node /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/scripts/health-prompt-hook.js",
   119â†’            "timeout": 5
   120â†’          }
   121â†’        ]
   122â†’      }
   123â†’    ]
   124â†’  }
   125â†’}
   126â†’```
   127â†’
   128â†’### Verification Rules
   129â†’
   130â†’Rules are defined in `config/health-verification-rules.json`:
   131â†’
   132â†’```json
   133â†’{
   134â†’  "version": "1.0.0",
   135â†’  "verification": {
   136â†’    "interval_seconds": 60,
   137â†’    "report_retention_days": 7,
   138â†’    "max_report_history": 1000
   139â†’  },
   140â†’  "rules": {
   141â†’    "databases": { /* ... */ },
   142â†’    "services": { /* ... */ },
   143â†’    "processes": { /* ... */ }
   144â†’  }
   145â†’}
   146â†’```
   147â†’
   148â†’Each rule defines:
   149â†’- `enabled`: Whether to run this check
   150â†’- `severity`: `info`, `warning`, `error`, `critical`
   151â†’- `check_type`: Type of health check to perform
   152â†’- `auto_heal`: Whether to attempt auto-healing
   153â†’- `auto_heal_action`: Action to execute if check fails
   154â†’
   155â†’## Data Files
   156â†’
   157â†’### Status File
   158â†’**Path**: `.health/verification-status.json`
   159â†’
   160â†’Quick status summary:
   161â†’```json
   162â†’{
   163â†’  "overallStatus": "healthy",
   164â†’  "violationCount": 0,
   165â†’  "criticalCount": 0,
   166â†’  "lastUpdate": "2025-11-10T06:11:21.553Z",
   167â†’  "autoHealingActive": false
   168â†’}
   169â†’```
   170â†’
   171â†’### Report Files
   172â†’**Path**: `.health/verification-history/report-{timestamp}.json`
   173â†’
   174â†’Detailed verification reports with:
   175â†’- All check results
   176â†’- Violation details
   177â†’- Auto-healing attempts
   178â†’- Recommendations
   179â†’- Performance metrics
   180â†’
   181â†’## Usage
   182â†’
   183â†’### Manual Verification
   184â†’
   185â†’```bash
   186â†’# Run one-time verification
   187â†’node scripts/health-verifier.js verify
   188â†’
   189â†’# Start daemon mode (continuous monitoring)
   190â†’node scripts/health-verifier.js start
   191â†’
   192â†’# Check current status
   193â†’node scripts/health-verifier.js status
   194â†’
   195â†’# View detailed report
   196â†’node scripts/health-verifier.js report
   197â†’```
   198â†’
   199â†’### Dashboard Access
   200â†’
   201â†’```bash
   202â†’# Start API server (port 3033)
   203â†’cd integrations/system-health-dashboard
   204â†’npm run api
   205â†’
   206â†’# Start dashboard (port 3032)
   207â†’npm run dev
   208â†’```
   209â†’
   210â†’Then visit: `http://localhost:3032`
   211â†’
   212â†’## How It Works
   213â†’
   214â†’### Typical Flow
   215â†’
   216â†’1. **User types prompt in Claude Code**
   217â†’2. **UserPromptSubmit hook fires** (health-prompt-hook.js)
   218â†’3. **Hook checks** `.health/verification-status.json` age
   219â†’4. **If fresh (<5 min)**: Adds health context, allows prompt
   220â†’5. **If stale (>5 min)**: Triggers async verification, adds "refreshing" context
   221â†’6. **Background verification runs**: Checks all services, databases, processes
   222â†’7. **Auto-healing activates**: Restarts any failed services
   223â†’8. **Status updated**: `.health/verification-status.json` written
   224â†’9. **Next prompt**: Shows fresh health data
   225â†’
   226â†’### Staleness Detection
   227â†’
   228â†’Data is considered **stale** if the file modification time is >5 minutes old.
   229â†’
   230â†’When stale:
   231â†’- Hook triggers async verification (doesn't wait for it to complete)
   232â†’- Claude receives: `ğŸ”„ System Health: Verification triggered (data was stale)`
   233â†’- Verification runs in background
   234â†’- Next prompt gets fresh data
   235â†’
   236â†’### Critical Failure Blocking
   237â†’
   238â†’If recent data shows **critical failures**:
   239â†’- Hook blocks the prompt with error message
   240â†’- User sees: `ğŸš¨ CRITICAL SYSTEM FAILURE DETECTED`
   241â†’- Prompt is NOT sent to Claude
   242â†’- User must fix critical issues first
   243â†’
   244â†’## Benefits
   245â†’
   246â†’### For Users
   247â†’- âœ… **No stale monitoring** - Every prompt ensures fresh health data
   248â†’- âœ… **No manual intervention** - System heals itself automatically
   249â†’- âœ… **Invisible when working** - <100ms overhead per prompt
   250â†’- âœ… **Clear feedback** - Health status appears in every response
   251â†’
   252â†’### For System Reliability
   253â†’- âœ… **Self-monitoring** - Health system checks itself
   254â†’- âœ… **Failsafe** - Can't start work with broken system
   255â†’- âœ… **Auto-recovery** - Failed services restart automatically
   256â†’- âœ… **No silent failures** - All issues logged and reported
   257â†’
   258â†’## Troubleshooting
   259â†’
   260â†’### Health hook not running
   261â†’
   262â†’Check settings:
   263â†’```bash
   264â†’cat ~/.claude/settings.json | jq '.hooks.UserPromptSubmit'
   265â†’```
   266â†’
   267â†’Verify hook file exists:
   268â†’```bash
   269â†’ls -la scripts/health-prompt-hook.js
   270â†’```
   271â†’
   272â†’Test hook manually:
   273â†’```bash
   274â†’echo '{"session_id":"test","prompt":"test"}' | node scripts/health-prompt-hook.js
   275â†’```
   276â†’
   277â†’### Verification data always stale
   278â†’
   279â†’Check if verifier is running:
   280â†’```bash
   281â†’ps aux | grep health-verifier
   282â†’```
   283â†’
   284â†’Run manual verification:
   285â†’```bash
   286â†’node scripts/health-verifier.js verify
   287â†’```
   288â†’
   289â†’### Health API not responding
   290â†’
   291â†’Check if running:
   292â†’```bash
   293â†’lsof -i :3033
   294â†’```
   295â†’
   296â†’Start manually:
   297â†’```bash
   298â†’cd integrations/system-health-dashboard
   299â†’npm run api
   300â†’```
   301â†’
   302â†’Test endpoint:
   303â†’```bash
   304â†’curl http://localhost:3033/api/health
   305â†’```
   306â†’
   307â†’### Auto-healing not working
   308â†’
   309â†’Check remediation logs:
   310â†’```bash
   311â†’cat .health/verification-history/report-*.json | jq '.metadata.auto_healing'
   312â†’```
   313â†’
   314â†’Verify rules have `auto_heal: true`:
   315â†’```bash
   316â†’cat config/health-verification-rules.json | jq '.rules.services'
   317â†’```
   318â†’
   319â†’## Performance
   320â†’
   321â†’- **Hook overhead**: ~50-100ms per prompt
   322â†’- **Verification runtime**: ~1-2 seconds for all checks
   323â†’- **Staleness threshold**: 5 minutes
   324â†’- **Dashboard refresh**: 5 seconds
   325â†’- **Auto-heal cooldown**: Configurable per action
   326â†’

# Documentation Styling Rules

This skill enforces comprehensive documentation standards across all projects.

## Critical Rules

### 1. NO LINE ART - EVER
**ABSOLUTE RULE**: Never create ASCII art or line-based diagrams in documentation.

**ALWAYS USE**:
- PlantUML for architecture diagrams, sequence diagrams, component diagrams
- Mermaid for flowcharts, state diagrams, simple visualizations

**WHY**: Text-based "line art" is not accessible, difficult to maintain, and looks unprofessional.

### 2. PlantUML Diagram Standards

**Location**: All PlantUML files MUST be stored in `docs/puml/`

**Style Sheet**: ALWAYS include the standard style sheet from coding project as the FIRST line after the opening tag.

**Layout Guidelines**:
- **Standard diagrams**: Prefer VERTICAL layouts to avoid excessive width
- Reason: Prevents users from zooming and scrolling horizontally
- Vertical scrolling is acceptable and preferred over horizontal scrolling
- Aim for narrow, tall diagrams that fit within typical screen widths

**Workflow for Creating PlantUML Diagrams**:

1. **Create the .puml file** in `docs/puml/` with proper naming
2. **Include standard style** - see reference documentation for the exact include syntax
3. **Design with vertical layout** - stack components top-to-bottom when possible
4. **Validate syntax** by attempting to render with plantuml checkonly flag
5. **Fix any errors** reported by plantuml validation
6. **Generate PNG** once error-free using plantuml command
7. **Move PNG to images folder** in docs/images/
8. **Reference in markdown** using relative path to the image

**IMPORTANT**: Never claim success until you've verified the PNG was created without errors.

### 3. Filename Conventions

**STRICT RULES** for ALL documentation artifacts (`.md`, `.puml`, `.png`, etc.):

**Permitted characters**:
- Lowercase letters: `a-z`
- Hyphens: `-`
- Numbers: `0-9`
- Extensions: `.md`, `.puml`, `.png`, etc.

**ONLY permitted exception**: `README.md` (capital letters allowed)

**Good Examples**:
- `system-architecture.puml`
- `deployment-flow.md`
- `api-endpoints.png`
- `README.md` (exception)

**Bad Examples**:
- Capital letters in names
- Underscores instead of hyphens
- CamelCase or PascalCase naming

### 4. NO INCREMENTAL NAMING

**CRITICAL**: Filenames and diagram text MUST represent the CURRENT STATE only, never showing evolution.

**FORBIDDEN PATTERNS** - Never use these suffixes or words:
- Version numbers or indicators
- Words suggesting improvement or change
- Words suggesting temporary status
- Words suggesting alternatives

**Why**: Documentation should reflect current state, not history. Use git for version history.

**Always**: Update the original file directly instead of creating variants.

### 5. Diagram Text Content

Text WITHIN diagrams must also be non-incremental:
- Component names should be simple and current
- Node labels should not indicate versions
- Actor names should not suggest enhancement status

## Implementation Checklist

When creating or updating documentation, verify:

- [ ] No ASCII/line art used (use PlantUML or Mermaid)
- [ ] PlantUML files stored in `docs/puml/`
- [ ] Standard style sheet included in .puml files
- [ ] PlantUML syntax validated with plantuml checkonly
- [ ] PNG generated successfully with plantuml
- [ ] PNG moved to `docs/images/`
- [ ] All filenames use lowercase + hyphens only (except README.md)
- [ ] No incremental suffixes in filenames
- [ ] No incremental labels in diagram text
- [ ] Markdown properly references images from `docs/images/`

## Tool Requirements

**Required tool**: `plantuml` must be installed on the system.

**Verification**:
```bash
which plantuml || echo "ERROR: plantuml not installed"
```

## Error Recovery

If PlantUML generation fails:

1. **Read the error message carefully** - PlantUML errors are usually specific
2. **Check syntax** - common issues include missing tags, unclosed quotes, invalid stereotypes, incorrect arrow syntax
3. **Validate include path** - ensure style sheet path is correct
4. **Test incrementally** - comment out sections to isolate problems

## Project-Specific Paths

### Standard Mode Style Sheet
Located at: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/puml/_standard-style.puml`

Use this path for regular documentation diagrams (12pt fonts, 2pt lines, vertical layout preference).

### Presentation Mode Style Sheet
Located at: `/Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/presentation/puml/_standard-style.puml`

Use this path for presentation diagrams (18pt fonts, 3-4pt lines, horizontal layout preference).

**IMPORTANT**: Both style sheets are named `_standard-style.puml` but are in different directories. The constraint monitor requires all PlantUML files to include a file named `_standard-style.puml`, so we use the same name in both locations but with different content optimized for each use case.

## PRESENTATION MODE

### When to Use Presentation Mode

Create a presentation mode version when:
- User explicitly requests "presentation mode" or "PPT version"
- Diagram will be used in PowerPoint or similar presentation software
- Diagram needs to be readable from distance (projector/large screen)
- Focus should be on key concepts, not detailed annotations

### Presentation Mode Workflow

When asked to create a presentation mode version:

1. **Copy source file** from `docs/puml/` to `coding/docs/presentation/puml/`
   - Keep the same filename (no suffix changes)
   - This is stored in coding project for reuse across all projects

2. **Rework the diagram** with these changes:
   - **Thicker lines**: All connections and borders become more prominent
   - **Increased font size**: All text becomes larger (18pt vs 12pt)
   - **Essential text only**: Remove verbose labels, keep only critical identifiers
   - **Remove annotations**: Delete all notes, legends, and explanatory text
   - **Horizontal layout**: Arrange for landscape PPT slide (left-to-right flow)
   - **Simplify**: Focus on core concepts, remove implementation details

3. **Update style sheet include** to presentation style:

   **Absolute path** (when referencing from any project):
   ```
   !include /Users/<USER_ID_REDACTED>/Agentic/coding/docs/presentation/puml/_standard-style.puml
   ```

   **Relative path** (when file is in the presentation/puml directory):
   ```
   !include _standard-style.puml
   ```

   Note: This is a different `_standard-style.puml` than the regular one - it's the presentation mode version with larger fonts and thicker lines.

4. **Validate and generate**:
   ```bash
   plantuml -checkonly coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.puml
   plantuml coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.puml
   mv coding/docs/presentation/puml/diagram-name.png coding/docs/presentation/images/
   ```

5. **Verify** the presentation PNG is created and suitable for PPT use

### Presentation Mode Characteristics

**Differences from Standard Mode**:

| Aspect | Standard Mode | Presentation Mode |
|--------|--------------|-------------------|
| Layout | Vertical (narrow, tall) | Horizontal (wide, landscape) |
| Font Size | 12pt | 18pt |
| Line Thickness | 2pt | 3-4pt |
| Text Detail | Comprehensive | Essential only |
| Annotations | Included | Removed |
| Notes/Legends | Present | Omitted |
| Purpose | Documentation | Presentation |
| Location | `docs/puml/` | `coding/docs/presentation/puml/` |

**Visual Optimization**:
- Thicker borders make elements visible from distance
- Larger fonts readable on projectors
- Horizontal layout fits 16:9 or 4:3 PPT slides
- Minimal text reduces cognitive load
- No legends/notes - slides should be self-explanatory or presenter explains

### Presentation Mode Example

**Original** (docs/puml/authentication-flow.puml):
- Vertical layout with detailed steps
- Includes notes about JWT validation
- Legend showing message types
- 12pt fonts, standard arrows

**Presentation** (coding/docs/presentation/puml/authentication-flow.puml):
- Horizontal left-to-right flow
- Only shows: User â†’ API â†’ Auth â†’ DB
- No notes or legends
- 18pt fonts, thick arrows (4pt)
- Labels: "Login", "Validate", "Query" (not "POST /api/v1/auth/login with credentials")

### Important Notes

- **Same filename**: Presentation versions use same name as original (no suffix)
- **Different location**: Stored in coding/docs/presentation/ tree
- **Not versioning**: This is a different presentation format, not a version
- **Reusable**: Presentation mode diagrams in coding/ can be used by all projects
- **Update both**: When updating a diagram, update both standard and presentation if needed

## Automation Opportunities

Consider creating helper scripts for:
- Batch validation of all .puml files
- Automated PNG generation on save
- Pre-commit hooks to enforce naming conventions
- Linting for incremental naming patterns
- Automatic presentation mode conversion

    14â†’

   107â†’## Integration with Health Verifier
   108â†’
   109â†’This dashboard consumes data from:
   110â†’- `scripts/health-verifier.js` - Health verification engine
   111â†’- `.health/verification-status.json` - Quick status file

   113â†’
   114â†’### Pre-Prompt Health Hook
   115â†’
   116â†’A UserPromptSubmit hook (`scripts/health-prompt-hook.js`) runs before every Claude prompt to ensure system health:
   117â†’
   118â†’**Behavior:**
   119â†’- Checks if verification data is stale (>5 minutes)
   120â†’- Triggers async verification if needed (non-blocking)
   121â†’- Provides health context to Claude in every response
   122â†’- Blocks only critical failures (prevents work when system is broken)
   123â†’
   124â†’**Configuration:**
   125â†’The hook is configured in `~/.claude/settings.json`:
   126â†’
   127â†’```json
   128â†’{
   129â†’  "hooks": {
   130â†’    "UserPromptSubmit": [
   131â†’      {
   132â†’        "hooks": [
   133â†’          {
   134â†’            "type": "command",
   135â†’            "command": "node /path/to/coding/scripts/health-prompt-hook.js",
   136â†’            "timeout": 5
   137â†’          }
   138â†’        ]
   139â†’      }
   140â†’    ]
   141â†’  }
   142â†’}
   143â†’```
   144â†’
   145â†’**Self-Monitoring:**
   146â†’The health verification system now monitors its own API server at `http://localhost:3033/api/health` and auto-heals if it goes down:
   147â†’- Check rule: `config/health-verification-rules.json` â†’ `services.health_dashboard_api`
   148â†’- Auto-heal action: `scripts/health-remediation-actions.js` â†’ `restartHealthAPI()`
   149â†’
   150â†’This ensures the health system itself is resilient and failsafe.
   151â†’

     1â†’# Process Monitoring System
     2â†’
     3â†’**Version**: 3.0
     4â†’**Last Updated**: 2025-10-15
     5â†’**Status**: Production
     6â†’
     7â†’## Overview
     8â†’
     9â†’The monitoring system provides unified process tracking, health monitoring, and automatic recovery for all coding project services. All process state is managed through the **Process State Manager (PSM)** as the single source of truth.
    10â†’
    11â†’## Architecture
    12â†’
    13â†’![Monitoring Architecture](images/monitoring-architecture.png)
    14â†’
    15â†’### Core Components
    16â†’
    17â†’#### 1. Process State Manager (PSM)
    18â†’**File**: `scripts/process-state-manager.js`
    19â†’**Purpose**: Centralized process registry with atomic operations and health tracking
    20â†’**Registry**: `.live-process-registry.json`
    21â†’
    22â†’**Features**:
    23â†’- Atomic file operations with proper locking
    24â†’- Session-aware service tracking (global, per-project, per-session)
    25â†’- Automatic dead process cleanup
    26â†’- Health check timestamp management
    27â†’
    28â†’#### 2. Global Service Coordinator
    29â†’**File**: `scripts/global-service-coordinator.js`
    30â†’**Purpose**: Service lifecycle management (start/stop/restart/health checks)
    31â†’
    32â†’**Features**:
    33â†’- Spawns and manages service processes
    34â†’- Automatic restart on failure with exponential backoff
    35â†’- Integrates with PSM for all state tracking
    36â†’- Self-registration with PSM for monitoring
    37â†’
    38â†’#### 3. System Monitor Watchdog
    39â†’**File**: `scripts/system-monitor-watchdog.js`
    40â†’**Purpose**: Failsafe monitor for coordinator health
    41â†’**Execution**: Via launchd every 60 seconds
    42â†’
    43â†’**Features**:
    44â†’- Monitors coordinator via PSM <USER_ID_REDACTED>
    45â†’- Restarts coordinator if dead or stale
    46â†’- Registers restarts with PSM
    47â†’
    48â†’#### 4. Session Management
    49â†’**Files**: `scripts/launch-claude.sh`, `scripts/psm-register-session.js`, `scripts/psm-session-cleanup.js`
    50â†’**Purpose**: Automatic service lifecycle tied to Claude sessions
    51â†’
    52â†’**Features**:
    53â†’- Session registration on Claude startup
    54â†’- Trap handlers for cleanup (EXIT, INT, TERM)
    55â†’- Automatic service termination on session end
    56â†’
    57â†’## Service Types
    58â†’
    59â†’| Type | Scope | Lifecycle | Examples |
    60â†’|------|-------|-----------|----------|
    61â†’| `global` | System-wide singleton | Managed by coordinator/watchdog | `vkb-server`, `constraint-dashboard`, `global-service-coordinator` |
    62â†’| `per-project` | One instance per project | Managed by coordinator | `transcript-monitor`, `trajectory-generator` |
    63â†’| `per-session` | Tied to Claude session | Auto-cleanup on session end | Custom session services |
    64â†’
    65â†’## Health Check Flow
    66â†’
    67â†’![Health Check Sequence](images/monitoring-health-check-sequence.png)
    68â†’
    69â†’### Watchdog Health Check (Every 60s)
    70â†’```
    71â†’1. Watchdog â†’ PSM: Query coordinator status
    72â†’2. PSM â†’ Registry: Read .live-process-registry.json with lock
    73â†’3. PSM â†’ Watchdog: Return service data
    74â†’4. Watchdog: Verify PID alive + health age < 120s
    75â†’5. If unhealthy: Kill stale â†’ Spawn new â†’ Register with PSM
    76â†’```
    77â†’
    78â†’### Coordinator Health Check (Every 15s)
    79â†’```
    80â†’For each managed service:
    81â†’1. Coordinator â†’ PSM: Check service health
    82â†’2. PSM: Verify PID exists + health timestamp fresh
    83â†’3. If healthy: Coordinator â†’ PSM: Refresh health timestamp
    84â†’4. If unhealthy: Attempt restart â†’ Register new PID with PSM
    85â†’```
    86â†’
    87â†’## Service Lifecycle
    88â†’
    89â†’![Service Lifecycle States](images/service-lifecycle-state.png)
    90â†’
    91â†’### State Transitions
    92â†’
    93â†’**Startup** (Unregistered â†’ Running):
    94â†’```javascript
    95â†’// Spawn service
    96â†’const child = spawn('node', [scriptPath, ...args]);
    97â†’
    98â†’// Register with PSM
    99â†’await psm.registerService({
   100â†’  name: 'service-name',
   101â†’  pid: child.pid,
   102â†’  type: 'global', // or 'per-project', 'per-session'
   103â†’  script: 'scripts/service.js'
   104â†’});
   105â†’```
   106â†’
   107â†’**Health Monitoring** (Running â†” Unhealthy):
   108â†’- Health checks via port, health file, or PID verification
   109â†’- Auto-restart with exponential backoff (1s, 2s, 4s, 8s, 16s, max 30s)
   110â†’- Max 5 restart attempts before marking as failed
   111â†’
   112â†’**Shutdown** (Running â†’ Unregistered):
   113â†’- Graceful shutdown unregisters from PSM
   114â†’- Session cleanup terminates and unregisters all session services
   115â†’- Coordinator registers/unregisters itself with PSM
   116â†’
   117â†’## Session Management
   118â†’
   119â†’![Service Startup Integration](images/service-startup-integration.png)
   120â†’
   121â†’### Session Lifecycle
   122â†’
   123â†’**1. Session Start** (`launch-claude.sh`):
   124â†’```bash
   125â†’SESSION_ID="claude-$$-$(date +%s)"
   126â†’export CLAUDE_SESSION_ID="$SESSION_ID"
   127â†’
   128â†’# Register session
   129â†’node scripts/psm-register-session.js "$SESSION_ID" "$$" "$PROJECT_PATH"
   130â†’
   131â†’# Setup cleanup
   132â†’trap cleanup_session EXIT INT TERM
   133â†’```
   134â†’
   135â†’**2. Session End** (Automatic):
   136â†’```bash
   137â†’cleanup_session() {
   138â†’  # PSM finds all services for session
   139â†’  # Terminates them (SIGTERM â†’ SIGKILL after 2s)
   140â†’  # Unregisters from registry
   141â†’  node scripts/psm-session-cleanup.js "$SESSION_ID"
   142â†’}
   143â†’```
   144â†’
   145â†’## API Reference
   146â†’
   147â†’### Process State Manager API
   148â†’
   149â†’#### Service Registration
   150â†’```javascript
   151â†’await psm.registerService({
   152â†’  name: 'my-service',
   153â†’  pid: 12345,
   154â†’  type: 'global', // or 'per-project', 'per-session'
   155â†’  script: 'scripts/my-service.js',
   156â†’  projectPath: '/path/to/project', // optional for per-project
   157â†’  sessionId: 'session-123', // optional for per-session
   158â†’  metadata: { ... } // optional custom metadata
   159â†’});
   160â†’```
   161â†’
   162â†’#### Health Checks
   163â†’```javascript
   164â†’// Check if service is running
   165â†’const isRunning = await psm.isServiceRunning('my-service', 'global');
   166â†’
   167â†’// Get service details
   168â†’const service = await psm.getService('my-service', 'global');
   169â†’// Returns: { pid, script, type, startTime, lastHealthCheck, status, metadata }
   170â†’
   171â†’// Refresh health timestamp
   172â†’await psm.refreshHealthCheck('my-service', 'global');
   173â†’```
   174â†’
   175â†’#### Session Management
   176â†’```javascript
   177â†’// Register session
   178â†’await psm.registerSession('claude-12345-1234567890', {
   179â†’  pid: process.pid,
   180â†’  projectPath: '/path/to/project'
   181â†’});
   182â†’
   183â†’// Cleanup session (kills and unregisters all session services)
   184â†’const result = await psm.cleanupSession('claude-12345-1234567890');
   185â†’// Returns: { cleaned: 3, terminated: [{name, pid}, ...] }
   186â†’```
   187â†’
   188â†’#### System Health
   189â†’```javascript
   190â†’// Get overall health status
   191â†’const health = await psm.getHealthStatus();
   192â†’// Returns: {
   193â†’//   totalServices: 10,
   194â†’//   healthyServices: 9,
   195â†’//   unhealthyServices: 1,
   196â†’//   byServiceType: { global: 3, 'per-project': 6, 'per-session': 1 },
   197â†’//   details: [...]
   198â†’// }
   199â†’
   200â†’// Cleanup dead processes
   201â†’const cleaned = await psm.cleanupDeadProcesses();
   202â†’// Returns: number of processes cleaned
   203â†’```
   204â†’
   205â†’## Troubleshooting
   206â†’
   207â†’### Services Not Showing in PSM
   208â†’
   209â†’**Symptoms**: `psm status` shows 0 services but processes are running
   210â†’
   211â†’**Solution**:
   212â†’```bash
   213â†’# Check running processes
   214â†’ps aux | grep -E "(vkb-server|coordinator|dashboard)"
   215â†’
   216â†’# Register manually
   217â†’CODING_REPO=$(pwd) node scripts/psm-register.js <name> <pid> <type> <script>
   218â†’```
   219â†’
   220â†’### Coordinator Not Restarting
   221â†’
   222â†’**Symptoms**: Watchdog reports dead coordinator but doesn't restart
   223â†’
   224â†’**Solution**:
   225â†’```bash
   226â†’# Check watchdog logs
   227â†’tail -50 .logs/system-watchdog.log
   228â†’
   229â†’# Run watchdog manually
   230â†’node scripts/system-monitor-watchdog.js
   231â†’
   232â†’# Verify PSM access
   233â†’CODING_REPO=$(pwd) node scripts/process-state-manager.js status
   234â†’```
   235â†’
   236â†’### Session Cleanup Not Working
   237â†’
   238â†’**Symptoms**: Services remain after session ends
   239â†’
   240â†’**Solution**:
   241â†’```bash
   242â†’# Check for orphaned processes
   243â†’ps aux | grep -E "(transcript-monitor|custom-service)"
   244â†’
   245â†’# Manual cleanup
   246â†’CODING_REPO=$(pwd) node scripts/process-state-manager.js cleanup
   247â†’
   248â†’# Verify session registration
   249â†’cat .live-process-registry.json | jq '.sessions'
   250â†’```
   251â†’
   252â†’### Registry File Locked
   253â†’
   254â†’**Symptoms**: "EEXIST: file already exists" errors
   255â†’
   256â†’**Solution**:
   257â†’```bash
   258â†’# Check for stale locks
   259â†’ls -la .live-process-registry.json.lock
   260â†’
   261â†’# Remove ONLY if no PSM operations running
   262â†’rm -f .live-process-registry.json.lock
   263â†’
   264â†’# Verify no PSM processes active
   265â†’ps aux | grep process-state-manager
   266â†’```
   267â†’

   334â†’## Startup Sequence
   335â†’
   336â†’1. **Pre-startup Verification**: `monitoring-verifier.js` checks system health
   337â†’2. **Session Registration**: `launch-claude.sh` creates session in PSM
   338â†’3. **Service Startup**: Coordinator ensures required services are running
   339â†’4. **Health Monitoring**: Continuous health checks (15s coordinator, 60s watchdog)
   340â†’5. **Session Cleanup**: Trap handlers clean up services on exit
